Empress

— Xu Benxi

Old uncles in the countryside, worried about the times and the chaos, admit that the true son of heaven has already been born. They believe that the future empress is only three years old and is herding cattle for others.

In fact, the emperor will ascend the throne sooner or later. Shanghai has launched a "xx empress" and then the Sino-Western joint empress election event. We should at least not deny that the emperor will be born in the near future. So, if the old uncles in the countryside could know that the empress has already ascended the throne, I think they would piously fast and bathe and come to Shanghai to kowtow three times and prostrate nine times to pay respects to the phoenix carriage.

Not only that, but with an empress, there will be a future emperor. At that time, with political unity, an edict will be issued to seek talents, and although the national crisis is severe, I'm afraid it won't call for a little brother to live and die, right? Then, the birth of the royal family should be the unique way to save the country. Are our Shanghainese smart enough?

Some people think that in China in an era of turmoil, even revolution is not enough, and this kind of activity fundamentally exposes the contradictions of the times. Well, that statement is clearly subjective. With a national character that is so strong in its desire for leadership, it is simply impossible not to produce an emperor. Simply put: with an empress, there will absolutely be no "midnight emptiness before the seat." Who wouldn't want to be Emperor Uncle?

We as citizens are always in danger of being beheaded. How about we be slaves? We want to shout "Long live the emperor, long live the empress!"

Long Novel

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Two: The Humble Room Blossoms with Fragrance—Secret Admiration for the Strong Man, the Quan Family Chooses a Good Match, and Scorns the Poor Girl

This conversation gave Zhao Weng an even better impression of the Jiang family. After returning to her room, she said to Guizhi, "This old man has a good heart, no wonder he raised a son who is a company commander." Guizhi immediately took the clothes in hand and hurried to make them, without any deep meaning in her mother's words. Seeing her daughter so eager to sew, Jiang couldn't be lazier than her. She also lowered her head, threading the needle and getting busy. Before twelve o'clock in the morning, she actually finished a robe. Guizhi burned the iron, ironing the clothes flat, and not even having time to eat, she wrapped the clothes in a piece of white cloth and sent them to the Gan family across the street. The owner of the Gan family, Gan Houzhi, was just coming out of the inner room when he met Guizhi in the courtyard. He smiled and nodded, saying, "Old girl, are you making clothes for our Jizhi again?" Guizhi said, "It's a robe for your second master Zhennian." Houzhi said, "He's not at home. You can leave it at your house, and I'll have your errand boy pick it up later. Why did you have to make a trip?" Guizhi heard that Jizhi wasn't home, so there was no need to send it to the inner room. Seeing the little errand boy standing next to him, she handed it to him and said with a smile, "Please give this to the second master, saying that the size of this dress was made according to the size of the last cotton robe. If it doesn't fit, take it to be altered. It's best if the second master wears it and lets me see it, so I can see where it doesn't fit and alter it there." The errand boy agreed and took the clothes inside. Guizhi couldn't see Jizhi, so naturally she went home. Houzhi watched Guizhi's shadow go far away. He didn't walk outside, but turned back to the inner room. His wife, Gan, was opening a box, looking for two good pieces of clothing to prepare to go to the city tomorrow to celebrate her elder brother's birthday at her maiden's home. Her elder brother had once served as a provincial governor, and although he was now retired and living in Beijing, he still had some political influence. Gan Houzhi, the director of the Western Suburb River Works Bureau, also owed his position to the influence of his elder maternal uncle. Mrs. Gan saw her husband walk in with an unhappy face and asked, "Who are you angry with?" Houzhi lit a cigarette and sat sideways on the back chair, lost in thought. After a long time, he exhaled a puff of smoke and said, "I laugh at our Jizhi for not being ambitious and falling for that old girl across the street. They visit each other every day, if not you coming, then me going." (20)

The Voice of National Salvation

Suggestions for an Open-Air University (Part 1)

— Zhang Yizeng

Reading is learning to be a person. Reading does not necessarily make you a person, but to be a complete person, you must read. Reading costs money. With money, you can read, and without money, you cannot read. This is aristocratic education. Popular education spreads knowledge, and my knowledge can be transformed into the knowledge of others, thus becoming a tool for society. The more widespread knowledge is, the more human happiness will increase.

An open-air university is a tool for popularizing knowledge. For this reason, I wrote a letter to Harvard University President Lowell, asking him to broadcast Harvard courses by radio, because the perfection of the school's curriculum is recognized by scholars around the world, and its high tuition fees are also a source of lament for poor students. Not only that, but people with jobs who are interested in research also suffer from not having time to attend school. I personally requested that Harvard's curriculum be promoted by radio. A week later, President Lowell's reply came, politely saying that public education also has its limitations. We know that Harvard is an aristocratic school, and the president is also aristocratic. After returning to my motherland, I always wanted to put this proposal into practice domestically. Open-air universities can not only avoid the recent popular student unrest, but also be very cheap in terms of economics. The school buildings do not have to be very grand, and management can also be much more convenient. Generally, students with pure character can no longer be affected by any political party, and can stop in the middle of the road. I have again petitioned the government authorities, explaining the pros and cons in detail, requesting that it be held, but under such a political situation, how can the matter of education invite an adult gentleman to take a look? Unfortunately, I can only study the plan of the Open-air University here with readers who are enthusiastic about education, hoping for criticism and sponsorship until success.

I have observed the current students, and they can be roughly summarized into two types. These two types are the most苦的students; one is those who have money to study but have no good school to enter; the other is those who have the ambition to study but have no money to enter school. The tuition fees of universities are too expensive now. An ordinary student in Shanghai needs about four hundred gold in expenses a year. If the family is poor, how can his family bear such a heavy burden? I often say that if Edison was in China, he would not be able to become a world-renowned scientist. Chinese newsboys can only sell newspapers for life. Very bitter Chinese newsboys, what opportunities do they have to study on their own! I visited a newsboy's club in Boston, which included reading, music, advertising, speeches, sports, etc. Even if they don't have a talent for invention, because the environment for learning is perfect, they can create a writer or inventor. I don't believe that among our 400 million Chinese people, there is not a single person like Mr. Ai? I lived in the countryside for two months this year and learned that there are many farmers with wisdom. I always want to give them the opportunity to develop their talents. In the ideal open-air university, we can create the Confucius, Mencius, Edison, Ford, and all the inventors of the 20th century.

The method of open-air university is much simpler than that of ordinary universities. All it needs are a few experts' audio discs and a few broadcasting stations. Each station serves as a department. First, invite experts to record the sound into an audio disc like an opera disc, and then send it to each department's broadcasting station for broadcasting. The poor, the rich, the old, and the young can all study. The rich can study at home behind closed doors, and students who have no money to buy electricity can go to the public education center to listen. On the one hand, please experts to compile books to make it easier for students to listen to lectures. Students can listen and read at the same time. If they have any questions, they can use the communication method to ask questions, or call or go to the public education center to see the assistant teacher, or consult the professor at the nearby university for explanation. The open-air university also has assistant teachers who answer students' questions to facilitate students' questioning. At present, China is in a process of constant change and progress. An open-air university like Harvard Road in the United States, Cambridge and Oxford in the United Kingdom, should be established. The open-air university can be divided into several departments, each department has an independent broadcasting station, and there are several assistant teachers who specialize in answering students with questions. If so, university education can have the hope of popularization.

Important News

Zhejiang Education Department Collects Middle School Graduation

Examination Questions Methods

Orders all public and private secondary schools in the province

Submit for reference before April 30

The Zhejiang Education Department used the previous year's (21st year) spring junior high school graduation examination as an opportunity to ensure that the examination questions were suitable for the teaching conditions of each school, and that the graduating students of each school could prepare adequately in advance. The "Measures for Collecting 21st Year Spring Junior High School Graduation Examination Questions" were formulated and circulated to all public and private secondary schools and above in the province for compliance. Now, in the second semester of the 21st year, both senior and junior high school levels have students graduating, and the number of classes and students graduating from each school is larger than the previous year. All examination matters are even more cumbersome, and preparations should be made as early as possible to ensure thoroughness. In reference to the previously issued methods, we have formulated new "Measures for Collecting Secondary School Graduation Examination Questions for the Second Semester of the 21st Year" and circulated them for compliance. The measures are as follows:

Measures for Secondary School Graduation Examination Questions for the Second Semester

(1) These measures are formulated in order to ensure that the examination questions are suitable for the teaching conditions of each school and that the graduating students of each school can prepare in advance. These measures are circulated to all middle schools in the province for compliance. (2) After receiving the order, each school should immediately have teachers of each subject formulate examination questions for each subject of the senior and junior high school examinations separately, and submit them to the department before April 30 for reference by the examination committee. Schools with only junior high schools may be exempted from formulating senior high school examination questions, and schools with only senior high schools may be exempted from formulating junior high school examination questions. Schools with graduating classes in the spring of this year that have already formulated and submitted junior high school examination questions in accordance with the previously issued "Measures for Collecting 21st Year Spring Junior High School Graduation Examination Questions" may be exempted from submitting junior high school examination questions. (3) Each school may conduct trial tests of the examination questions formulated by itself in the graduating classes of the school in order to prepare. (4) The examination questions for each subject are not limited to the teaching materials of the last semester, and should be based on all teaching materials of the three years, with uniform distribution without adding weight. (5) The scope of the examination questions for each subject is based on the "Provisional Curriculum Standards" promulgated by the Ministry. (6) The examination questions for each subject are not limited to the textbooks used by the school, and should refer to the various textbooks approved by the current Ministry of Education for mixed questions. (7) The examination questions for each subject, except for Chinese and foreign languages, may be formulated separately for various types of composition questions. Mathematics may be formulated separately for ordinary question types. All others should use test question types, without limiting the number of various test question types, such as the right and wrong method, the selection method, and the filling method. (8) The content of the test is not limited to the memory of facts. All that belongs to understanding, reasoning, etc., can be tested. (9) The examination questions should be attached with answers. Both the examination questions and answers must avoid being cumbersome and strive for accuracy. (10) Physical education, in accordance with the Ministry of Education's interpretation, will be examined and graded by the original schools and sent to the department for review. No examination questions need to be formulated. If necessary, sample examination questions will be stipulated separately.

Ministry of Education Supervisor's Inspection Report on Jiangxi Education (Part 1)

The Ministry of Education believes that Jiangxi has been greatly affected by the communist bandits in recent years, and the education must have been greatly affected. In order to understand the actual situation, the Ministry of Education specially sent Supervisor Zhong Daoqi to inspect the province's education in February of this year, and pay attention to the promotion of vocational education, for about a month. A total of more than fifty institutions were inspected, including three specialized schools, eighteen secondary schools, seven social education institutions, eighteen primary schools, and two education bureaus. Supervisor Zhong has completed his work and returned to Beijing, and has completed the整理reporting. The content is divided into seven parts: general outline, specialized schools, vocational schools, secondary normal schools, primary schools, social education, and opinions on the improvement of education in Jiangxi. It is quite concise. Here, we disclose the important points:

1. The teaching equipment of each specialized school, except for the medical school, can barely be used, and the rest feel lacking. Especially the factory and farm are the most difficult. The promotion of agricultural specialized schools is almost not held.

2. Graduates of each specialized school, except for medical and civil engineering students, have no problem finding jobs. The rest are not easy to arrange. Especially agricultural science is the most difficult. Half of it is because the internship is not sufficient, and half of it is because the social business is very undeveloped.

3. The internship problem of each specialized school should make full use of the holidays, and send students to various hospitals, coal mines, railway bureaus, and other vocational institutions for long-term apprenticeships in order to obtain real experience.

4. Each specialized school should select those departments that are difficult to run or have poor job prospects from the existing departments, stop recruiting as necessary, and change to more socially needed departments. At the same time, unnecessary subjects should be deleted and practical training should be given.

5. The purpose of the senior high school attached to each specialized school is to prepare for further studies, but it should also give students practical vocational training according to their economic and academic conditions, so that they can be self-reliant.

6. Except for the Second Vocational School, which has no problem finding jobs for business students, most vocational schools are regarded as a way to prepare for further studies. Therefore, there are too many ordinary subjects and insufficient time for vocational subjects, and practice is not thorough.

7. There are too many vocational subjects included in each department of each vocational school. Often one person has to learn four or five different types of occupations. As a result, there are many but not精, affecting job prospects. Moreover, the length of each department is the same and cannot be extended or shortened according to the nature of the occupation.

8. Although the existing departments of each vocational school are not few, there is still a lack of architecture, drawing, furniture production, nursing, and commercial design. Attention should be paid to this.

9. Girls' vocational supplementary schools have many subjects and are run like elementary schools, which is not the original intention of setting up the school. Ordinary subjects should be reduced and vocational training should be concentrated. The length of time should also not be too long.

10. Most vocational schools feel a lack of teachers, especially in skill subjects. It seems that technical personnel from the vocational industry should be hired as practical teachers as much as possible to emphasize practice.

11. Provincial No. 2 Middle School, Girls' Middle School, and private Xin Yuan, Gan Sheng, Bao Ling, Ru Li, Tong Wen, and other middle schools have achieved good results in running schools, and the equipment is passable. The school spirit of No. 1 Middle School was originally excellent, but recently it has become slightly relaxed due to the change of principal. The better trained is the Provincial No. 2 Middle School.

Regulations for Secondary and Normal Schools (4)

Second Table of Weekly Teaching and Self-Study Hours for Each Subject in Senior High School

(Explanation)

(1) This curriculum is only applicable to the senior high school departments of secondary schools established in special areas that require Mongolian, Hui, Tibetan, or a second foreign language.

(2) The second foreign language refers to Russian, German, French, Japanese, etc.

(3) Senior high school departments of secondary schools that apply this curriculum should first submit a special report through the competent educational administrative authority to the Ministry of Education for review and approval.

(4) If senior high school departments of secondary schools that apply this table encounter special difficulties, they may appropriately reduce English by one or two hours per week, but must submit it to the competent educational administrative authority for forwarding to the Ministry of Education for record.

(5) The total number of hours for high school students' daily classes, self-study, and extracurricular activities is stipulated to be ten hours, calculated as sixty hours per week.

(6) In addition to class time each day, one hour is allocated for morning exercises and extracurricular activities, and the remainder is for self-study.

(7) Both on-campus self-study and extracurricular activity time must be supervised and guided by teachers.

(8) All on-campus self-study must be attended by both boarding and day students.

(9) In special circumstances, if necessary, the Ministry of Education may approve the non-establishment of English courses, with one type of second foreign language replacing it.

Article 26. Secondary schools established in special areas that require Mongolian, Hui, Tibetan, or a second foreign language may reduce the teaching subjects of hygiene, ethics, drawing, and music in the senior high school department.

Article 27. Secondary schools may establish vocational subjects to adapt to local needs and for experimental education purposes, but must first submit the established subjects and equipment status to the Ministry of Education for approval.

Article 28. Secondary school curriculum standards will be determined separately.

Article 29. Secondary school textbooks must adopt those edited or approved by the Ministry of Education. Teachers' self-compiled teaching materials must conform to the curriculum standards set by the Ministry, and all teaching materials must be submitted to the competent educational administrative authority at the end of each semester for review and reporting to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 30. Teaching of each subject should actively use textbooks, adopt local and temporary supplementary teaching materials, and focus on experiments and practice.

Article 31. Teachers should pay attention to observing students' personalities, and should inspire their ability to observe and think, and their spirit of automatic research.

Article 32. Students in the final grade of secondary school may use holidays for sightseeing travel, but it must not hinder class time, and the cost shall be borne by the students themselves.

Chapter 6 Moral Education

Article 33. Secondary school moral education should follow the educational purpose and implementation policies of the Republic of China, cultivate young people, the national morality of "loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, faith, righteousness, and peace," and foster a spirit of courage and perseverance and a habit of discipline.

Article 34. According to the implementation policies stipulated for labor practice, secondary school students, in addition to labor course assignments, must be assigned to undertake internal school organization, cleaning, fire prevention, and road repair, afforestation, water conservancy, sanitation, literacy campaigns, etc. in the vicinity of the school. The number of school workers should be reduced to a minimum.

Article 35. Secondary school principals and all teachers are responsible for moral education, and must lead by example, adopt group training and individual training to guide students in all in-class and extracurricular activities.

Article 36. Each class in secondary school shall have one class teacher, selected from among the full-time educators in that class, who shall be responsible for the moral education and management matters of each class.

Article 37. The principal and full-time teachers should, in principle, reside on campus and live with the students.

Article 38. Secondary school student dormitories must have teachers residing in them to be responsible for management.

Article 39. Secondary school students should wear uniforms in accordance with the student uniform regulations.

The reproduction of uniforms should be based on the wear and tear of the uniforms of general students, and students should not be required to make new uniforms every semester or every year.

Article 40. Students who are absent from class and lazy in self-study or labor assignments in secondary school should have points deducted from their conduct grades.

Article 41. Secondary school moral education standards will be determined separately.

Article 42. Measures for the moral education, management, rewards, and punishments of secondary school students

The educational administrative authorities of each province and city shall stipulate the outline and submit it to the Ministry of Education for approval and implementation. Each secondary school shall formulate detailed rules in its school regulations based on this outline and submit them to the competent educational administrative authority for approval and implementation.

Zhou Fo-hai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department

Inspecting Education in Southern Jiangsu (1)

Arrived in Danyang at 1:00 PM on the 21st, and immediately inspected the Bureau and the People's Education Center

(Special Correspondent in Danyang) Zhou Fo-hai, Director of the Jiangsu Education Department, believes that local education in this province urgently needs investigation to promote it. He personally inspected the northern Jiangsu area at the end of last year, provided detailed guidance, and made many reforms. Therefore, education in Tongzhou and Rugao counties has greatly improved in recent months. Director Zhou believes that although southern Jiangsu is a culturally developed area, there are still many areas that need guidance. Therefore, on the 21st of this month, he led Chen Xi-fang, the head of the Second Section, Bai Ju-tan, the head of the Third Section, Yi Jun-zuo, the chief editor, and staff member Li Xin-min of the department, to various counties along the Nanjing-Shanghai railway line for on-site inspections. He arrived in Danyang at 1:00 PM that afternoon, and immediately took a car into the city and stayed at the Lianhu Hotel. County Magistrate Wang Ji-wu, Director of Education Wang Ming-ji, and others rushed to the hotel after hearing the news. After lunch, they went to the private Zhengze Girls' School in the county to inspect the teacher's mathematics class, the teacher's drawing class, the third grade's singing and games class, the sixth grade's Three Principles of the People class, the fifth grade's Chinese class, and embroidery, sewing, kindergarten, and other classes. He inquired in detail about the school's administration and students' extracurricular activities from Principal Lü Feng-zi, and gave many instructions on the implementation of livelihood education. Then, he went to the county normal school to inspect the middle school's physiology and hygiene class, the middle school's composition class, the middle school's business class, and the teacher's craft class. He inquired in detail about the school's implementation of the department's policy of combining education and training and raising the level of standards. Afterwards, he went to the county library to check various books, and asked questions about the mobile library and reading group organization, paying attention to how to arouse the public's interest in reading and encourage literacy education. He detoured to the Education Bureau to examine administration, finances, and read the reports of various supervisors, and reviewed various records. At this time, the wind became stronger and stronger, the spring cold was particularly severe, and the sky was getting late. Director Zhou and others went to the county People's Education Center to examine everything, inquired about the progress of the department's standard work, and briefly described the situation to the county party headquarters and the county government. He returned to the residence at 7:00 PM. After dinner, he reviewed the student grades sent by various schools until late at night. During today's inspections, he paid attention to the sales and reading situation of the "Jiangsu Education" and "Jiangsu Students" monthly magazines. It is reported that he will continue to inspect tomorrow and leave Danyang for Changzhou at 6:00 PM.

(Zhenjiang, 22nd) Zhou Fo-hai departed on the 22nd to inspect education along the Nanjing-Shanghai railway line.

Local News

City Education Association Holds Council Meeting

Important Proposals Regarding Recent Situation

Establish Four National Defense Policy Lectureships

Actively Promote Fundraising for Shanghai School Aircraft

Write to Aviation Administration Requesting Aircraft Performance in Shanghai

The Shanghai Municipal Education Association held its eighth council meeting at the Chinese Arts and Crafts Society at 3:00 PM yesterday. Zhou Fei-cheng, Xu Ze-yu, Huang Zao-xiong, Tao Bai-chuan, Chen Ji-cheng, and others attended, while Zhang Xiao-tian, Wang Yong-zhi, Mao Yun, and others were present as observers. Zhou Fei-cheng chaired the meeting and Chen Bang-yan served as the recorder. The following major cases were resolved: (1) Promoting the purchase of the Shanghai School No. 1 military aircraft. It was resolved that the Aviation Association should be notified that the membership fees recruited by the education sector team leaders hired by the Aviation Association this time, and the membership fees recruited by other team leaders within the education sector, should be allocated to the Shanghai School aircraft project to purchase the Shanghai School aircraft. (2) Chen Pin-yi suggested requesting the central government to transfer one or two aircraft to Shanghai for performance and display, and inviting all children in Shanghai to visit and promote aviation. It was resolved to write to the Municipal Aviation Association and the Aviation Administration, requesting the dispatch of one fighter, bomber, and reconnaissance aircraft each to Shanghai for performance on a regular basis, and to display them in Longhua for several days for public viewing and promotion. (3) The Fourth District Party Headquarters requested the Association to send personnel to reorganize the Fourth District Education Association. It was resolved that a new election was imminent, so there was no need for reorganization. (4) Investigate and determine that the terms of office of the secretaries of the Education Associations in various districts have expired, and convene a general meeting of members to hold a new election as soon as possible. It was resolved to pass the motion. (5) Determine the Association's proposals regarding the recent situation. It was resolved to stipulate the following principles: (1) Military action against the Japanese army should shift from defense to offense. Troops along various passes in Northeast China should attack simultaneously and cooperate to recover lost territories. (2) Absolutely refuse to conclude any peace treaty with Japan before the lost territories in Northeast China are recovered. (3) Centralize military power and unify military orders to enhance the effectiveness of resisting Japan. (4) Implement national mobilization, popularize and intensify the anti-Japanese movement. (5) The Sino-Japanese tariff reciprocity treaty will not be renewed after its expiration. (6) Establishing National Defense Policy Lectureships. It was resolved to establish four lectureships: (1) Military National Defense Policy, (2) Economic National Defense Policy, (3) Educational National Defense Policy, (4) Diplomatic National Defense Policy, and to hand them over to the Guidance Section for handling. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

High School Graduates During Summer Vacation

Can Take the Central Military Academy Entrance Exam

The Preliminary Examination in the City Remains Scheduled on the Original Date

The Central Retake Examination is Postponed to Late June

Regarding the Shanghai preliminary examination for the 10th class of recruits to the Central Military Academy, which is being organized by the Shanghai Education and Public Security Bureaus, has been reported in various newspapers. It is now reported that the Bureau has received instructions from the Municipal Government, roughly approving the training directorate's consultation. The date of the retake examination for the 10th class of recruits to the Central Military Academy has been postponed to late June to avoid the time crunch for remote provinces and regions. High school students graduating this summer, although not yet graduates at the time of the preliminary examinations in various provinces and cities, already possess the academic ability of high school graduates, which is in accordance with Article 2, Section 1 of the Academy's recruitment rules, which stipulates the qualification for application: high school graduation or equivalent to high school graduation level. They should be allowed to take the preliminary examination for this year's recruits, but a certificate must be issued by the school to avoid confusion. It is also reported that the Academy's regulations stipulate that applicants for the Shanghai preliminary examination must be registered in the city or be foreign students studying in the city, and a certificate must be issued by the school where they are studying for verification.

Sports

400-Meter World Record Holder

Carr Seriously Injured

Car Collision Causes Hip and Knee Injuries

Doctors Officially Announce Inability to Compete Again

Carr's Record is 46.5 Seconds

(Philadelphia, USA, 21st) Bill Carr, the world record holder for the 400-meter dash at 46.5 seconds, has had doctors officially announce that Carr will not be able to reappear on the track.

Last Saturday, Carr was seriously injured in a car collision. At the time of the accident, Carr was standing on the running board of a car, which collided with another car. Carr was thrown into the street, and his knee and hip bones were severely injured.

Carr set a new world record in the 400-meter dash at the Los Angeles Olympics last fall with a time of 46.5 seconds. Prior to that, Carr had declared that he would no longer participate in track and field championships, but was willing to participate in the American track and field team traveling to Europe this year. Unfortunately, this accident occurred, and Carr will not be able to fulfill his wishes.

Carr's statement of retirement is as follows: "I sincerely wish to participate in the American track and field team traveling to Europe this summer, but after returning, I will abandon my sportswear and shoes for other uses. I will devote all my time to my career. I do not believe that a person cannot be both a businessman and an athlete, so I have decided to retire from the track and field."

Tianjin-Shanghai Interport Football Match

Shanghai Team Scheduled to Go to Tianjin on April 12

Two Matches to be Played in Tianjin, Returning to Shanghai on the 18th

Western Union Modifies Constitution and Rules, Appoints Committee Members

Western Union Officially Announces Recent Results for Each Group

The Shanghai Western Football League accepted an invitation from the Tianjin Western Merchants Football Club last winter to send a team to Tianjin this Easter for the Tianjin-Shanghai Interport Match. It has now been learned that the League has decided to send a team north from Shanghai on the 12th of next month. The following is a summary of the latest news from the Western Union.

Shanghai Interport Team Scheduled to Go to Tianjin

In the past few years, the Tianjin Interport Football Team has come to Shanghai three times to compete, but due to various reasons, the Shanghai team has not yet reciprocated. Therefore, this Easter, the Shanghai Western Football League has decided to send a team north to compete in the Interport Match. The league's various group matches are almost all completed, making it a good opportunity to accept the Tianjin invitation. Therefore, the club is making every effort to prepare to select a representative team to travel north by express train on the 12th of next month and return to Shanghai by train on the 18th. They will stay in Tianjin for a week to prepare for two matches. Further details will be announced later.

Committee Members Appointed to Revise Constitution and Rules

The current constitution and rules of the Shanghai Western Football League have been largely in use since 1927. After the experience of the recent season, it has been felt that revisions are necessary in many areas. Therefore, the Western Union has established a special committee to revise the constitution, with members being Whitelegg, Facheux, and Marshall, and Haimson as the committee secretary. They will consider the constitution and report back to the Western Union, no later than the beginning of August this year, with suggestions to revise the constitution to meet current needs. The suggestions will be discussed at the annual general meeting in early September.

Yesterday Jiangnan University Basketball

Jinnnan Doubles Over Fudan

New Facilities at Jinan Sports Field

(Jinan, 22nd) The provincial sports field's children's basketball tournament will draw lots today, and the games are scheduled to begin on the 26th. The five-week tournament aims to encourage children's interest in sports. The field has decided to add a children's playground with sports equipment, games classes, sports associations, tour group variety shows, and sports meets. Photography will be used to record progress, display charts, and add sanitary game posters to make the field a children's paradise. The field has newly purchased 37 acres of land and decided to add four volleyball courts, six basketball courts, and one football pitch each. The existing various ball fields will be converted into ten tennis courts.

US President Pays Attention to Silver Problem

丨White House Meeting Necessary to Maintain丨

Reuters, Washington, 21st. President Roosevelt and congressional leaders held a meeting at the White House last night. The restoration of silver also had some glimmer of hope during the meeting. Senator Wheeler said that the silver problem was discussed at the meeting. According to the opinion at the time, it seemed necessary to maintain silver. Senator Pittman, the author of the Pittman Plan and other silver proposals, said that President Roosevelt told congressional leaders at the meeting, "He is deeply concerned about restoring silver prices and purchasing silver." Pittman said that he had scheduled a discussion on the silver problem with the Secretary of the Treasury within a day or two. After the discussion, he would discuss it with President Roosevelt again. Pittman told President Roosevelt last night that he and others would have an opportunity to discuss with the President within a few days. He would see the establishment of a law to prevent criticism or attack on the American gold standard, while restoring the original purchasing power to allow silver coins to circulate in the world.

Explanation of US Silver Export Ban

According to a Washington dispatch from the previous day, regarding President Roosevelt's orders on March 5 and 9 to ban silver exports, the Secretary of the Treasury stated on the 16th, "There are no restrictions on silver for the delivery of commercial goods," and "The ban is limited to those who withdraw silver for collection." According to the interpretation, there are no restrictions on silver for the delivery of goods. Only those who withdraw large amounts of cash for storage abroad will be prosecuted.

American Cotton Falls by 20 to 30 Points

Yesterday, American cotton prices were weak due to a lack of major buyers, a sluggish Wall Street, and unfavorable news from Liverpool. Futures prices fell by 24 to 29 points, and spot prices fell by 30 points. British cotton futures fell by 3 to 4 points, and spot prices rose by 2 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 1 point. Indian cotton trading was suspended. The original telegram is recorded on the left. (Telegraph on the 21st)

Grains: Flour Futures Weak Near-Term, Higher Far-Term

Yesterday, the flour market showed weakness in all months in the morning. Foreign wheat prices continued to fall by about 0.2 to 0.3 taels. The current month hovered around 1.766 taels due to slight sales. Distant months showed sluggishness due to small imports of foreign wheat, but trading was not active, falling only 0.0025 taels compared to the previous day. In the afternoon, the current month continued to hover. The Tianjin group slightly sold off, while Xin Da, Shen Da, and others slightly replenished their stocks, showing mutual exclusion. Distant months were stable due to the lack of activity in spot foreign wheat caused by tight exchange rates. Factories also did not release new supplies, leading to a recovery in sentiment. However, overall trading was slow, lacking vitality. As a result, the current month fell by 0.0025 taels compared to the previous day, April rose by 0.0025 taels, May rose by 0.0075 taels, and June, July, and August rose by 0.005 taels.

Wheat Market Almost Stalled

Yesterday, the wheat market was unusually stagnant. Only the current month saw some trading in a few carts in the morning, with the rest being empty bids. In the afternoon, only the current month and August saw slight trading, with no other activity. The quiet atmosphere was truly rare. As the current month approached delivery, it was heard that Ding Tai had prepared to deliver 30 to 40 carts of goods. However, it was reported yesterday that foreign wheat had already been loaded onto the docks, preparing for spot sales, so many offset their positions on the exchange. As a result, the current month rose by 0.01 taels compared to the previous day, and August also rose by 0.01 taels.

Sugar Market: Dutch Raw Sugar Prices Rising

Yesterday, sugar prices were as follows: Association #24 coarse white sand at 15.1 taels, top-grade RA at 15.3 taels, #20 medium white sand at 14.65 taels, #18 at 14.45 taels, all up by 0.05 taels. #8 Dutch raw sugar at 11.8 taels, up 0.1 taels. Chang Xing offered a batch of Guanghua-produced green-letter cotton white sugar at 15.3 taels. On the local firms' side, the Chaozhou group offered 500 to 600 bags of Chao Qing at 8.68 taels, and lower grades at 8.5 to 8.45 taels (excluding broker commission). Taikoo sugar prices remained mostly unchanged, with B at 15.95 taels, CW at 15.85 taels, DY at 15 taels, and HX at 15.7 taels. Although Hainan raw sugar prices were called higher, no transactions occurred.

Free Discussion

The People's Duty

— Qi Fan

The people's duty lies in abiding by laws and paying taxes. Consequently, the duty of the government, which governs and controls the people, lies in enforcing laws and collecting taxes. The quality of a people is judged by their ability to abide by laws and pay taxes. Similarly, the quality of a government is judged by its ability to enforce laws and collect taxes. I dare say that our current government is indeed a good government.

The government is composed of officials, and a good government has good officials. A good official is one who can carry out the necessary tasks of a good government, that is, enforce the government's laws to govern the people and collect taxes. I believe that all our current officials are also good officials; they can all fulfill their duties and will ensure that the people are law-abiding and dutiful. Here, being dutiful means paying taxes, and being law-abiding is, of course, a brief way of saying abiding by the laws.

It is enough for the people to fulfill the duties they should fulfill. There is no need to interfere in other matters. For example, once taxes are paid, that is the end of the matter. There is no need to ask about how the money is used. Because the people are always just the people. If they do things that the people should not do, they will violate the laws of the country and become bad and treacherous people. Good officials will certainly not bear this and will certainly correct them. This is also one aspect of their enforcement of the law.

The government's affairs are naturally handled by the government. There is no need for the people to participate in or interfere. If there is a government, and the government's affairs still require the people to assist, then what is the use of the government? Therefore, in matters such as resisting Japan, the government always instructs the people to remain calm and contribute financially. Because the people's duty really does not go beyond these two paths. Remaining calm is abiding by the law, and contributing financially is taking out money. Being able to take out money and also abide by the law, the people's duty is fulfilled. There is no need for anything else.

However, recently, the government announced the organizational law of the National Political Council and the principles of the member election law. This is really a bit illogical. If the word "National" is interpreted as "People", then if there is something called "National" other than "People", then it must be clearly defined to avoid confusion with the people, lest there be a danger of passing off dross as gold. Because the people's duty is as described above, they are definitely not worthy to participate in any politics.

If the "National" who participate in politics are indeed the people, then there is really a great danger. First, because it will damage the government's authority. The people were originally governed, and it was enough to pay taxes. They have always been humble and submissive. If they are once raised up to stand as equals with the government, will they not despise the government's authority in the future? Politics is a strange thing. If you get your hands on it, it can change people's minds. Therefore, if the originally docile people are given the right to participate in politics, they will become unruly and fierce, making them difficult to govern. Wouldn't that be annoying?

Moreover, the people have not asked for any right to participate in politics. The people now only ask to pay less taxes and for fewer laws to be promulgated. Now, giving them the great power of participating in politics is too ill-considered. This kind of method is very likely to make the people forget their duty to pay taxes and instead think about interfering in the government's actions. This should really be paid attention to. Fortunately, it has only been passed by the Central Standing Committee and still needs to be reviewed by the Legislative Yuan. But the matter is already like riding a tiger, and it is feared that it is bound to be implemented. Then, one can only hope that this Political Council is nominal and not real, so as to avoid the danger of disrupting the laws of the country.

This is very important when drafting the regulations. As long as a little effort is made, it can be done. I think our drafting committee members are all good officials, and they are all intelligent, so they must have made preparations in those areas.

Remembering Joseph

— Cao Juren

The sensational case in Shanghai of the Italian Uveugu accusing Xue Jinyuan of seducing his son Joseph has given me deep feelings. Joseph studied with me for four months seven or eight years ago. He was very intelligent and had a good physique, but unfortunately, his environment was not good. His father, an Italian, was extremely extreme in his emotions. He wanted Joseph to receive a Western education, but after entering a Western school, he soon came out. His mother, from Suzhou, was too docile. She wanted Joseph to receive an Eastern education, hoping that I would teach him things like the "Three Character Classic," but after four months, he was not seen entering a formal elementary school. For the past ten years, Joseph has been neither Western nor Eastern, and the result is that he has not received any education. I once said to a friend: "It is not okay for children in Shanghai to not receive an education. If you don't educate him, there is a big school - the society of Shanghai - that will educate him. By the time you find that the tree trunk is already bent, there is no way to save it." Sure enough, Miss Xue Jinyuan came to be Joseph's professor. Even without seduction, her daily instruction and polishing work produced very good results. To let a sixteen- or seventeen-year-old child tumble in the palm of a courtesan is a terrible thing!

Family education in Shanghai has developed strangely. Some people regard their children as precious orchids and trees, and they must be planted in front of the steps. Each family hires a tutor to receive the most old-fashioned education. This kind of child education, isolated from society, means that children can never participate in community life, just like flowers and plants locked in a room, never seeing the sun. A sudden storm will knock them to pieces. The fate of precious orchids and trees is often like this. Some people treat their children as wild horses, letting them run wild in society. First, there is alleyway education, then street education, and finally playground and dance hall education. Hustling, messing around, loitering... a complete set of "three-education" textbooks creates a large group of young rascals. Children are like weeds on the edge of a rice paddy, trampled by cattle and sheep, leaving no vitality. This is how the previous generation harms the next generation, a cycle of cause and effect without end! Miss Xue Jinyuan has taught Joseph, and Joseph has taught many misses, expanding the position of social news in the newspapers every day. The worsening of syphilis is spreading to the entire society of Shanghai. How can this not be chilling!

Please, people from all walks of life in Shanghai, do not take this matter as a trivial joke. This is a major issue of child education facing us! In the Soviet film "Road to Life", it says at the beginning: "A child without education is a destroyer of the construction of the new society." Shanghai is already full of gangsters, rascals, beggars, and all kinds of vagrants. Now, still letting them constantly teach and train the reserve team, how can we avoid the fate of total collapse!

Ah Q is Always Alive

— Qi Yu

This is a small protest: Who says Ah Q is dead? He is indeed still alive and well, and his luck is in full swing.

Those who doubt this will surely ask in surprise, "Where's the evidence?"

Well, look—

Didn't the × month × day ×× newspaper carry a speech by a certain official, saying that "The violent sun's artillery fire is not to be feared; within ten years, Japan will surely have a major revolution"?

What is the difference between saying this and someone who is unable to take revenge on their enemy and hopes that their enemy will get sick?

Even three-year-old children know that this is a pathetic, cowardly, and powerless statement, yet it comes from the mouth of a high-ranking official. I am really a little worried for him. Why doesn't he say something readily available? If he were to say: "Japan has recently suffered a major earthquake and will soon withdraw its troops and return the lost territories, which is not a problem," wouldn't that be more likely to make the foolish common people believe and feel at ease?

I remember that every time Ah Q was beaten, he would mutter, "I was only beaten by my son!" to console himself and seek spiritual victory. When I was young, I only found it funny, but now I realize that Ah Q's spirit is our national philosophy.

Who says Ah Q is dead? Ah Q is always alive!

Full-Length Novel

The Crossroads of Time and Love

— Zhang Guanping

"That Pastor Liao forced him to go! Old Liao wanted him to tell Old Ha to increase his salary from January next year."

"How much salary does Pastor Liao get every month?"

"Fifty yuan. He asked for an increase to eighty yuan. But Old Ha didn't agree. Later it was reduced to seventy yuan, but he still didn't agree. Old Liao then reduced it to sixty yuan..."

"Then Old Ha is too stingy."

"Isn't he! Old Liao has been working in the church for twelve or thirteen years. Old Ha still won't budge even if he only adds ten yuan." Every time Madam Cao said "Isn't he!", she would slightly tilt her head, and her lips would move very quickly, which further reduced her beauty and the first condition of womanhood, gentleness.

"Then what did Old Liao do?"

"With Old Ha being so unfeeling, Old Liao couldn't bear to ask directly. So, he asked Shiguang to act as if he were advising him on his own, asking Old Ha to add five yuan to his salary from January next year. Shiguang went to the church on the day before yesterday and yesterday, but he didn't meet that foreign devil, and he just wasted the fare. Mr. Lin, Christmas is coming soon, they are busy, so Shiguang went to the church early this morning again, hoping to catch him before he left. He has been running around for nothing for Old Liao's five yuan." "Religious people are really stingy!"

"Not just stingy, completely cruel! There's no future in working for religious people. I often regret it. I'm not saying bad things about Mr. Cao, but I really married the wrong person! I never knew he was so useless!"

After she said this, she looked at Haiquan with a flirtatious smile. Haiquan thought again, "I really don't deserve this."

Twenty-Eight

After sitting foolishly in Cao Shiguang's house for a while, he remembered the chewing gum in his pocket, and he hurriedly took it out.

"This is something I bought along the way out of boredom, but it's still special..."

"What is it?"

Madam Cao didn't stand on ceremony at all and took the packs of chewing gum.

"...Oh, I thought it was something else. Mr. Lin, Chewing Gum? I loved to eat it when I was in girls' school!"

"Mrs. Cao, you also know Chewing Gum?"

Haiquan was a little surprised. How could she be so fashionable, have eaten Chewing Gum, and even said that she had lived in a girls' school? He wondered which girls' school it was.

Random Notes on Reading

— Wang He

Recently, because the Japanese dwarfs have been bullying our Chinese nation too much, I am indignant and deeply hope that some literary works that can promote national consciousness will emerge. At the very least, there should be some publications like "National Literary Selections," so that "words have power, and the national spirit can be awakened." A few days ago, I saw a newspaper advertisement for "National Literary Selections" compiled by the Chinese Literature Department of Jiangsu Provincial Zhenjiang Middle School. Overjoyed, I went to a certain bookstore on Simalu Road to buy a copy. Upon returning, I burned a good incense in front of Yue Wumu's portrait and carefully read it. The first article I read was The Biography of Shi Kefa (selected from the History of Ming), which contains the following passage:

Shiying (referring to Ma Shiying) then entered his duties that day and proposed dividing Jiangbei into four garrisons: Liu Zeqing, Earl of Dongping, administered Huaihai and Huaibei, managing the military affairs of Shandong Province; Gao Jie administered Xusi, stationed in Sishui, managing the military affairs of Kaigui; Liu Liangzuo administered Fengshou, stationed in Linhuai, managing the Chenqi region; Jingnan Earl Huang Degong administered Chuhe, stationed in Luzhou, managing the Guanggu region. This passage confused me: Liu Zeqing and Gao Jie both managed the military affairs of a province, while Liu Liangzuo and Huang Degong only managed a certain region, without "military affairs of a province" below. Could it be that the commander-in-chief was killed in battle outside Shanhaiguan while resisting the Manchurian puppet state? This reminded me of a former tutor who, when reading the Great Learning,

Knowing where to rest, you will have determination; having determination, you will be able to calm down; being calm, you will be able to be at peace; being at peace, you will be able to deliberate; being able to deliberate, you will then achieve. He was greatly puzzled by the lack of a "achieve" character at the end of the last sentence. Later, I ran to another private school and saw that the tutor there was troubled by the extra "achieve" character in the Great Learning, with nowhere to put it (because his punctuation was: Knowing where to rest, you will have; having determination, you will be able; being calm, you will be able; being at peace, you will be able; being able to deliberate, you will be able; achieve...). He happily said, "Having searched far and wide, I found it with ease! The 'achieve' character I was missing was actually here!" It's a pity that the two "commanders-in-chief" in "National Literary Selections" are nowhere to be found for the time being. Reading on,

Kefa had no son. He left instructions for Shi Dewei to be his successor. He had a younger brother, Kecheng, who became a Jinshi in the sixteenth year of Chongzhen and was promoted to Shujishi; when the capital fell, he surrendered to the rebels; when the rebels were defeated, he returned south. Kefa requested that he be punished, but Prince Li (note: a person's name line is added next to the two characters "Prince Li" in the original text) spared him for Kefa's sake and ordered him to support his mother. Kecheng then lived in Nanjing. Later, he lived in Yixing and died after forty years.

It turns out that Shi Kefa, who is considered a "national hero," could not uphold righteousness by killing his own relatives. He asked Prince Fu to pardon his unworthy brother (li means law, putting him to law means putting him to li). On the contrary, he asked Prince Fu to ignore his brother's betrayal and surrender to the rebels. Someone like this, who perverts the law for personal gain, is actually given a biography in the History of Ming, pretending to be a loyal minister of the Ming Dynasty and a national hero of China. It is truly unjust and wrong! (Please forgive me for quoting the idiom "acting important." I really didn't intentionally offend Mr. Shi Kefa. I say this because Mr. Shi Kefa is already dead. He won't accuse me of "acting important," send a letter demanding an apology, or even spend money to publish an advertisement. Similarly, Mr. Shi Kefa will not hire a lawyer to sue the editor of "National Literary Selections" in court.) Also, I have never seen the name "Prince Li" in the History of Ming or other unofficial histories of the late Ming Dynasty. I record it here to await further research.

Our Army Holds an Advantage Outside Lengkou

Enemy Troops Fiercely Attack Xiaojiayingzi Mountain Temple

Our Troops Charge Repeatedly and Finally Repel the Enemy

The Enemy-Occupied Blockhouse at Jielingkou is Surrounded

Yiyuan Fortress Enemy Repelled and Guarded by Militia

Enemy Aircraft Reconnoitered Our Shihe Position This Morning

Leizhou: An enemy detachment, consisting of a brigade of infantry, cavalry, and artillery, with more than a hundred armored vehicles and tanks as the backbone, launched a fierce attack on Xiaojiayingzi Mountain Temple, about thirty miles outside Lengkou, at 11:00 AM on the 22nd. Our [illegible] Division Commander personally supervised the troops and fought bravely, charging back and forth more than ten times. By 2:00 PM, the enemy was unable to withstand the attack and retreated. At 3:00 PM, the enemy reinforced with reserves and launched a counterattack. The fierce battle lasted until 6:00 PM, when the enemy still could not withstand the attack and retreated in disarray. Our army captured three tanks and many guns and cannons. Inspections revealed the battle was as fierce as the Xifengkou and Gubeikou battles. The enemy suffered heavy casualties, and our army also suffered some casualties. It has been confirmed that Company Commander Meng Zhankui and Platoon Leader Ma Dengying were killed in action. Morale is extremely high, preparations are thorough, and the enemy will not be allowed to cross the border a single step. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Beiping) After He Zhuguo's headquarters moved to Leizhou, there were no changes in the front-line troops. Only the defense troops stationed at Jiumentou, Qindao, and other places were reassigned under Yao Dongfan's command. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Linyu: On the 21st, the enemy repeatedly attacked our army at Yiyuan Fortress, but were repelled by our army and the militia. At about 7:00 AM today, the enemy reinforced with about 2,000 mixed troops of the Japanese and puppet (Li Jichun) forces from Suizhong, and began to bombard our army's positions with more than a dozen aircraft and more than a dozen cannons for about two hours, followed by an infantry assault. Our army immediately dispatched [illegible] troops to reinforce. As of 2:00 PM in the afternoon, the fierce battle was still ongoing. There were five or six close-quarters combat engagements today. The intensity of the fighting and the ferocity of the battle were unprecedented. In the end, our army defended the key points and fought calmly, defeating the superior enemy. It is estimated that about two to three hundred enemy soldiers were killed, and our army suffered no less than a hundred casualties. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Beiping) The enemy at Yiyuan Fortress has been repelled and is guarded by the militia [illegible]. The area around Shimenzhai Laojunding is also guarded by the militia. The two Northeast Miao and Yao brigades are in the rear. This area is quite important. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Tianjin) A telegram from Leizhou states that the enemy took advantage of our troop rotation around Jielingkou and Yiyuan Fortress and launched fierce attacks on the 20th and 21st, creating a momentary crisis. Later, a certain unit of our troops who withdrew from outside the Guan unexpectedly arrived behind the enemy. The enemy, attacked from both sides, collapsed in disarray, and we recovered our original positions. The various passes along the Great Wall were heavily bombed by enemy aircraft, and the people fled in droves. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

(Beiping) Miao Brigade's Zhao Lei Battalion defected and led the enemy in a counterattack on Yiyuan Fortress, but were defeated by Zheng Guilin's troops. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Linyu: A portion of the enemy at Jielingkou occupied a blockhouse on the Great Wall. Our [illegible] army surrounded it on all sides, cutting off communication. However, this enemy stubbornly resisted and used aircraft to deliver supplies. A large number of enemy troops rushed to reinforce them. There was a fierce battle at about 6:00 AM today, but the enemy ultimately failed to succeed. They are currently still surrounded by our army. (Special dispatch, 22nd)

(Beiping) Enemy aircraft were spotted reconnoitering our Shihe position this morning. The enemy troops on the opposite bank are restless, and the situation is extremely tense. Our side is fully prepared. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

The Enemy Continues to Increase Forces at Gubeikou

| A Military Expert Speaks |

The Japanese Army May Invade Chahar and Suiyuan

(Beiping) The enemy forces at Gubeikou increased by more than a thousand on the 20th, by a regiment (about two thousand) on the 21st, and by forty cannons on the 22nd. They will launch a fierce attack on our army. Our army is prepared to fight to the death. (Special dispatch, 21st)

(Beiping) A certain military expert said that after occupying the key passes of the Great Wall, the Japanese army will invade Chahar and Suiyuan to the west, or may temporarily avoid Beiping and Tianjin to avoid international opposition. Therefore, in the near future, the Japanese will launch fierce attacks on Xifengkou, Lengkou, etc. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

The Training Supervision Department Establishes the

National Military Training Committee

(Nanjing) The Training Supervision Department is implementing military training in schools, reaching 178 schools in seventeen provinces. The scope is vast. However, in the past, the operating system was directly between the schools and the Department, without an intermediate organization. Achievements may not be significant. Therefore, it is proposed to establish a National Military Training Committee in the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to create a comprehensive organization. A draft of eleven provisional regulations has been prepared and submitted to the National Government for promulgation and implementation. The National Government has approved the record after submitting the report and instructed the Department to jointly issue a circular with the Ministry of Education for implementation. (Central News Agency dispatch, 23rd)

The South Manchuria Railway Company

Will Build Two New Railways

Reuters Tokyo, 23rd: Minister of Colonial Affairs Nagai has submitted a new financial procedure plan for the South Manchuria Railway to the Special Committee of the House of Representatives. According to Nagai, the South Manchuria Railway plans to build three new railways in Manchuria and one new railway in Korea. In addition, the Raxing Port in Korea will also be rebuilt this year. The entire procedure requires a total expenditure of 100 million yen. The cost of building Raxing Port is 26.1 million yen. The new railway in Korea will take two and a half years to build. The necessary funds will be raised by increasing capital and issuing bonds.

This Morning's Central Standing Committee

Discusses the Issue of the Premier of the Executive Yuan

Shao Yuanchong is Additionally Appointed as a Member of the North China Office

(Nanjing) The 23rd Central Standing Committee discussed the issue of Wang's reinstatement. Because Wang's consent must first be sought, no concrete decision was made. It is faintly heard that Wang instructed Gu Mengyu to convey to the Central Committee before going to Shanghai that he was going to Shanghai for business and would return to Nanjing in a day or two. He still firmly declined to resume the premiership. Gu presented a report at today's Standing Committee. It is heard that the result was the appointment of Sun Ke and Gu Mengyu to go to Shanghai to urge Wang to return to Nanjing immediately. (Special dispatch, 23rd)

Wang Jingwei Arrives in Shanghai This Morning

Still Humbly Declines the Premiership of the Executive Yuan

Wang Says His Visit to Shanghai is to Visit Song and Urge Him to Take Office

And Telegrams the Central Committee to Formally Appoint Mr. Song

Song's Attitude is Firm and He Still Urges Mr. Wang to Resume His Post

Wang Jingwei, Premier of the Executive Yuan, accompanied by his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, and Vice Minister of Railways, Zeng Zhongming, etc., took the night train from Nanjing last night at 11:00 PM and arrived at Zhenru Station at 7:50 AM this morning, proceeding directly to his residence on Bo Shi Road for rest. Wang stated that his visit to Shanghai was to meet with Song Ziwen, Acting Premier of the Executive Yuan, and ask Song to formally take the post of Premier of the Executive Yuan. After Song agrees, Wang will immediately return to Nanjing and then go north on schedule to comfort the front-line soldiers and meet with Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang. Otherwise, he plans to stay in Shanghai temporarily, expressing his determination. After Wang got off the train, he telegraphed the Central Standing Committee, proposing to formally appoint Song as Premier of the Executive Yuan. The details are as follows:

(Arriving at Zhenru Station) Our reporter drove to Zhenru Station at about 7:00 AM this morning. Besides the staff, there was no one in the station, and there were no arrangements for heavily armed military police security. Wang's secretary arrived at the station to greet him at about 7:40 AM. The train arrived at the station at 7:50 AM, and Wang and his wife, Zeng Zhongming, etc., got off the train and took a car directly to his residence on Bo Shi Road for rest.

(Wang's Remarks) Wang was wearing a gray suit when he got off the train at Zhenru Station. His face was rosy and his spirits were good. Our reporter immediately stepped forward to talk with him. According to Wang, regarding the issue of the Premier of the Executive Yuan, he firmly resigned because his illness had not yet healed and he could not handle the heavy workload. The Central Standing Committee will formally discuss this matter today. He has telegraphed to request the appointment of Mr. Song Ziwen as Premier of the Executive Yuan. The reason for his visit to Shanghai this time is to meet with Mr. Song and urge him to take office in person. After Song agrees, he will immediately return to Nanjing within a few days, and then go north on schedule to comfort the front-line soldiers and meet with Military Affairs Committee Chairman Chiang. Otherwise, he will stay in Shanghai temporarily and wait for the matter to be resolved.

(Visiting Song Ziwen in Person) Wang went to Song's residence at 9:30 AM, simply dressed, and sincerely expressed to Mr. Song that he really could not handle the heavy workload due to his illness and earnestly requested him to take on the difficult task and accept the post of Premier of the Executive Yuan. However, Mr. Song still declined humbly, saying that his physical strength was also weak and his blood pressure was still high, so he firmly refused to take office and refused to act as an agent again. The two discussed for a total of 30 minutes, but they still humbly declined each other and no results were achieved. Wang then bid farewell and left.

(Zeng Zhongming Expresses) According to Zeng Zhongming, Vice Minister of Railways, who accompanied Wang to Shanghai, Mr. Wang refused to resume his post because his body could not support the heavy workload. The purpose of his visit to Shanghai this time was to persuade Mr. Song to go to Nanjing and take office to avoid resentment and harm the country. After Wang resigned from the post of Premier of the Executive Yuan, it did not mean that he would completely ignore state affairs, but would work in the Central Party Headquarters. As for whether Wang would return to Nanjing immediately, it depends on the situation of the contact with Vice Premier Song. The Central Committee held a Standing Committee meeting this morning to discuss this matter. If this matter is resolved, then Mr. Wang can enter Nanjing in one or two days. If Song still declines, the Central Committee has no intention of promoting other candidates. The time for the meeting between Wang and Chiang has not yet been determined. All parties intend to promote Chairman Chiang to be the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force to unify military power, but this has not been heard in Nanjing. He will return to Nanjing by night train tonight.

(Telegram to the Central Committee) After arriving in Shanghai this morning, Wang telegraphed the Central Committee, proposing to the Central Standing Committee to formally appoint Acting Premier Song as Premier of the Executive Yuan. The original text read: To the Central Executive Committee, Zhao Ming resigned from the post of Premier of the Executive Yuan in August of last year. The Central Committee decided to order him to concentrate on serving in the Central Party Headquarters, and Vice Premier Song Ziwen was acting as Premier of the Executive Yuan. In mid-October, Zhao Ming applied for leave due to the severity of his illness and inability to serve in the Central Party Headquarters. He was granted a three-month leave to go to Europe for treatment. Recently, due to the fall of Rehe, he returned to Nanjing with all his strength, hoping to share this difficulty with his comrades. However, at this time, with all his efforts, he can only offer suggestions in the Central Party Headquarters at any time. As for the post of Premier of the Executive Yuan, the work is heavy and the responsibility is great. It is not a pity for the sick body, but the failure of the work and the misguidance of the country will be deeply blamed. Since entering Nanjing, he has repeatedly explained in detail to his comrades and hoped to be understood. Today is the date of the Central Standing Committee meeting, and he dares to sincerely request that the committee understands his sincerity and formally appoint Comrade Song Ziwen as Premier of the Executive Yuan, cancels the word "acting," so as to specialize in responsibility and unified perception. Zhao Ming will still be in the Central Party Headquarters as long as he has breath, following his comrades to face the national crisis together. He respectfully submits this proposal and awaits a public decision.

(Song Ziwen Firmly Declines) The reporter interviewed Acting Premier Song Ziwen at 10:30 AM this morning. According to Song, Mr. Wang came here this morning, saying that he would not return to his original position as Premier of the Executive Yuan and ordered him to continue to be responsible. However, he firmly stated that he could not take the position in order to specialize in finance. The position of Premier of the Executive Yuan should of course be resumed by Mr. Wang. In this period of increasing national crisis, if the whole country unanimously urges Mr. Wang, he can reluctantly take on the heavy task and overcome the national crisis together. The Central Committee's policy towards Japan is to resolutely resist and never compromise. There are often rumors of direct negotiations and compromises with Japan, which are not true. It is very clear that Japan cannot even accept the League of Nations resolution, and is about to withdraw from the League. How can it be possible to make concessions to us? And how can our government submit to a strong enemy and sign a treaty that would cut off the lifeblood of the country? Anyone who compromises with Japan will be abandoned by the whole country. He (Song) has no special knowledge of the military situation in North China, but he knows that the transfer of defenses in Leizhou is purely a necessary strategic move. The Japanese are clamoring to disturb Beiping and Tianjin, and we are also prepared. If the enemy recklessly invades Beiping and Tianjin, they will be met with a head-on blow. As for the recent promotion of the former Chairman to be the Commander-in-Chief of the Army, Navy, and Air Force to unify power, Chairman Chiang himself only seeks to win the war against the enemy and does not seek to take on the title.

(Chu Talks About Wang Seeking Medical Treatment) The Central News Agency in Nanjing telegraphed on the 23rd, that Premier Wang and his wife, Ms. Chen Bijun, and Deputy Railway Minister Zeng Zhongming, etc., took the night train to Shanghai on the evening of the 22nd, as reported in the newspapers. The Central News Agency reporter visited Chu Minyi at the Executive Yuan on the morning of the 23rd and asked when Wang would return to Nanjing. Chu replied that Wang had returned to the country, and travel between Nanjing and Shanghai was common for various premiers and committee members. As far as he knew, the purpose of this trip to Shanghai was to seek medical treatment and test blood. It is difficult for ordinary doctors to draw blood from veins for analysis. Dr. Nol, who accompanied Wang to Europe, also returned to Shanghai with Wang, so Wang is still asking him for treatment.
