Japan is Deciding

Rehe Economic Work

(Changchun) The Japanese-Manchu authorities have announced the following regarding economic work in Rehe Province: (1) Transportation: The roads in Rehe Province are worse than in other provinces, which greatly inconveniences economic development. The first priority is to construct roads. Construction of the two main roads between Beipiao and Chengde, and between Chaoyang and Chifeng, has already begun. Other lines will be started gradually. (A) Regarding telegraph and telephone: First, a new telegraph line between Chaoyang and Chifeng will be built. Then, a complete telegraph network will be established in the major settlements within the province, and some telephone lines will be opened at the same time. (B) Regarding postal services: The post offices in major settlements have already been placed under the administration of the Manchurian government. (2) Finance: Opium purchasing offices will be established in Chengde, Lingyuan, Chaoyang, and Chifeng. The opium cultivation tax, which was previously ten yuan per mu, will be reduced to five yuan. The annual opium production is estimated at about 300,000 guan. A. Regarding taxes: Indirect taxes will go to the central government, while direct taxes will be used for provincial expenses. B. Regarding customs duties: Customs offices will be established in Chengde, with branch offices at the forty gates along the Great Wall. C. Regarding finance: The Central Bank of Manchuria will establish branches in Chaoyang, Chengde, and Yifeng to recall the currently circulating banknotes. Furthermore, there are considerable prospects for the reserves of natural resources such as coal and oil. The military has recently decided to dispatch a large survey team. (23rd dispatch from Tong News Agency)

Germany's Active Diplomacy

Movement to Recover Overseas Territories

Japan's Refusal to Relinquish Mandated Islands

Causes Extreme Concern to German Government

Reuters, Berlin, 22nd: The issue of returning Germany's overseas territories has now become an important part of Germany's foreign policy. The National Socialist government attaches great importance to Japan's declaration that even if Japan withdraws from the League of Nations, it will not return the Pacific islands formerly under its mandate. Today, official sources stated that this issue can only be resolved by the Council of the League of Nations and the Mandates Commission. If the Council of the League of Nations and the Mandates Commission can handle this matter, the German government will take the position of safeguarding all the interests of Germany's territories.

China United News Agency, Tokyo, 23rd: The Japanese Foreign Ministry received a report from its embassy in Germany stating that the German government issued a statement yesterday saying that the issue of the mandated rule of the South Pacific islands must be resolved by the Council of the League of Nations and the Mandates Commission. The German government has decided to assert its demands in these two bodies and will not make any separate representations to Japan. Although the Japanese government has withdrawn from the League of Nations, it has decided to continue participating in the Mandates Commission. Therefore, after withdrawing from the League of Nations, it will face even more serious conflicts with various countries in the League of Nations. The Japanese Foreign Ministry considers this statement to be an important issue and will carefully study how to deal with it.

Amidst Talk of German-Austrian Union

Calls for Restoration in Germany Resurface

Hitler's Dictatorship Seems Inevitable

Reuters, Berlin, 22nd: The Standing Committee of the Reichstag met today and the National Socialist Party's six votes defeated a motion to release eleven Social Democrat deputies still in detention. The Bavarian People's Party did not vote. The newly elected Prussian Parliament, with a National Socialist majority, met today and, after confirming the appointment of the government, immediately adjourned indefinitely. Amid cheers, National Socialist Deputy Dr. Kubel spoke of the National Socialist Party's ambition to unite Germany and Austria into a great nation. A deputy from the German National People's Party said that he hoped for the day when the Hohenzollern dynasty would be restored to rule Germany, which was also met with applause. The Reichstag will reconvene tomorrow and is expected to pass a bill granting dictatorial powers to Hitler's cabinet, allowing it to govern without the Reichstag. Tonight, the official organs of the National Socialist Party have already issued a warning that if the Reichstag does not accept the bill, it would be tantamount to declaring war on the National Socialist Party, and that the result would not only harm the opposition parties (the Centre Party, the Bavarian People's Party, and the Social Democratic Party) but also the voters. The National Socialist Party of the Saarland today sent a telegram to Chancellor Hitler protesting the fact that the police in Saarbrücken yesterday forcibly removed the party flag from the National Socialist headquarters.

France Raises Many Objections

Progress in Four-Power Cooperation is Slow

French Prime Minister May Visit Rome

Reuters, Paris, 22nd: French Prime Minister Daladier may visit Italian Prime Minister Mussolini in Rome to discuss the Four-Power Pact between Britain, France, Italy, and Germany. However, France has raised many objections to this matter, which has slowed progress. France believes that the trend of the Four-Power Pact could divide European countries into several categories and damage the nature of the League of Nations, as member states of the League of Nations enjoy equal rights within the League.

Disarmament Conference Adjourns

Small Entente Countries Greatly Shaken

Poland and Romania Protest

France Takes a Wait-and-See Attitude

Havas, Geneva, 22nd: The adjournment declaration of the Disarmament Conference, jointly drafted by Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson, British Prime Minister MacDonald, and Foreign Secretary Simon, has greatly shaken people here. Some view this declaration directly as the first move in four-power politics in Europe. Representatives of most secondary countries clearly stated that this matter has created a bad impression on their respective governments and criticized the British, saying that they want to use the Rome and Paris talks as an excuse for the adjournment of the Disarmament Conference. According to last December, after the five powers reached a compromise on the issue of equality of armaments, the General Committee did not consider it appropriate for a small number of countries to privately handle the matter outside the Disarmament Conference. Yesterday's announcement by Henderson and others about the adjournment news again raised doubts about the great powers' willingness to negotiate privately. Some say that Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu intends to express his views clearly in the name of the Little Entente countries, and Polish representative Raczkiewicz will certainly lodge a protest again. Henderson is well aware of this mentality, so his attitude tomorrow will be more reserved, unlike the frankness of yesterday's press release. It is likely that the adjournment will be requested by the British delegation or the Italian delegation, and Henderson will not advocate it himself. France will take a wait-and-see attitude. If the adjournment is indeed decided, the French representative will request that restrictions be placed on the adjournment time and that the various specialized committees continue their work. Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu will soon go to Paris to state his views in the name of the Little Entente countries.

Havas, Athens, 22nd: Greece has expressed its approval in principle of British Prime Minister MacDonald's disarmament plan, but has raised some reservations on specific issues.

France Deploys Border Defenses

Franco-Belgian Cooperation is Important

Havas, Paris, 22nd: The Army Committee of the Senate met, chaired by Mr. Messimy. Prime Minister and Minister of War Daladier, accompanied by General Gamellan, Chief of the General Staff of the Army, and Mr. Le Foch, Director of the Engineering Department, attended the meeting. They explained the construction of the northern border defenses. The Prime Minister made a detailed and clear report and stated that the cooperation between France and Belgium is close and sincere, and their relationship is extremely important.

Liangdigoumen

Sun's Troops Fight Bloodily With the Enemy

Destroy Three Tanks and Kill Many Enemies

(Beiping) Sun Dianying reported by telegram to Ping on the 20th that at dusk on the 19th, the enemy on the Liangdigoumen front attacked our left flank with over 3,000 cavalry and over 50 tanks and armored vehicles, and charged fiercely at our positions with a large number of troops, supported by over 20 field guns firing simultaneously. Our officers and soldiers calmly resisted, holding their fire until the tanks were close, then charged with broadswords and hand grenades. The enemy could not withstand the attack and retreated. The most tragic aspect of the battle was when our officers and soldiers were fighting to capture the tanks. The enemy inside the tanks fired machine guns and used mountain gun shells. It was only after over 90 officers and soldiers were killed that three tanks were destroyed, over 170-180 enemies were killed, and a company commander named Yamanouchi Dairō was captured. He will be sent to Ping soon. As of the time of the telegram, fierce fighting was still ongoing. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Trans-Baikal

Rumors of Mutiny in Russian Army

(Harbin) News of a mutiny by Soviet Russian soldiers in Trans-Baikal, on the Siberian border, has now spread to Harbin. Although the Russian authorities are trying hard to investigate, the news was eventually leaked. According to a report from a reliable Japanese source, the rebel soldiers were Russian soldiers from the 55th Regiment stationed in Da Uria, and their mutiny took place at the end of February. They were subsequently suppressed by the Russian authorities, and many officers were arrested. It is heard that other regiments also sympathized with the rebel soldiers. The cause of the mutiny of the 55th Regiment was the poor and inadequate food and the fact that the soldiers had not been paid for three months. The soldiers accumulated grievances, which eventually erupted. Da Uria was formerly part of Mongolia, located between the Yablonovy Mountains and the Argun River. (23rd Reuters Dispatch)

At the same time, President Roosevelt also intends to merge the Justice Department's Secret Service, the Bureau of Internal Revenue's Investigation Division, and the Communications Division, and the Postal Service's Inspection Division into a new agency to implement his plan to reorganize government spending.

Huge Amounts of Russian Goods Imported

According to today's Japanese-language Shanghai Nippo, since the restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia, various goods from the Soviet Russian Federation have been continuously shipped to China, distributed from Shanghai to various cities and markets throughout China, which is very prosperous. The main goods being dumped are timber, kerosene, cotton cloth, coal, glass, wheat, wheat flour, and fish. According to the import manifest of the third Russian merchant ship, the Khedivstroy, which arrived on the 21st, the following goods were imported: (1) 5,000 tons of kerosene, 500 tons of wheat, 1,000 tons of timber, and 1,000 tons of cotton cloth, with a total value of approximately 20 million taels. These goods have already been unloaded at the 16th Pier. Except for timber and coal, which are directly managed by Russian merchants, kerosene is sold by Guanghua Company, and cotton cloth is managed by Dachunghua Company.

Bodyguard Shouts Kidnapping

Scaring Away Large Numbers of Kidnappers

Zhang Yunjie Not Captured by Bandits

Kidnappers Made Detailed Preparations in Advance

Some Selling Wonton, Others Pulling Rickshaws

Fled in Panic, Abandoning Handguns

Kidnapping of Zhou Xitang Also Done by Such Gangs

Zhang Yunjie, a native of Ningbo, fifty years old, lives at No. 359, Gaoen Road, French Concession. He has been running a hardware store in Fengtian and is moderately wealthy. He owns a car with license plate number 6577 and hires Xue Sichuan, a native of his hometown, as a driver. Because kidnapping cases are now prevalent, for defense, he hired Qiu Zhaoshan from Hebei as a bodyguard to accompany him in and out. Zhang likes Peking opera and often goes to the Zhengyi Opera House at No. 184, Shandong Road, Nanjing Road, to learn Peking opera. This has become a habit. Yesterday morning, before 2:00 a.m. (late on the 22nd), Zhang, his wife, and Qiu Zhaoshan went to the Zhengyi Opera House again. When they came out at 2:15 a.m., just as they left the entrance of the opera house, suddenly six or seven kidnappers, each carrying a handgun, stepped forward and shouted threats, intending to kidnap Zhang. At that time, Qiu Zhaoshan, unprepared, did not have time to draw his gun to resist. He had no choice but to shout, "Kidnapping!" The bandits were startled by the shout, fearing that the police would arrive, and dispersed in all directions, abandoning Zhang. The relevant General Patrol Room received a report and immediately ordered Chinese detectives Xie Shuiquan, Pang Ruiqing, Geng Debiao, etc., to rush to the scene to search, but the bandits had disappeared without a trace. After investigation by Detective Xie and others, it was learned that the kidnappers' procedures this time were quite thorough. They had all disguised themselves in advance, some as wonton vendors, others as rickshaw pullers, pre-positioned in the small alley next to the Zhengyi Opera House to avoid the attention of law enforcement officers. The failure of the bandits this time was all thanks to Qiu Zhaoshan's shout. The bandits, in their hasty escape, left behind a handgun with nine bullets at the corner of Nanjing Road and Henan Road, in front of the Henglida Watch Company. The detectives picked it up and found that the gun number was 443803. The gun was owned by the Russian bodyguard Wei Weisharov of Zhou Xitang, a comprador of the Lao Gong Mao Foreign Company. Recently, Zhou suddenly encountered many kidnappers near the Dada Pier in the Chinese area, who attempted to kidnap Zhou. Zhou resisted, and the bandits immediately opened fire, wounding Zhou and killing the bodyguard Wei on the spot. They also robbed Wei of his gun and scattered in all directions. Zhou died of his injuries at Tongren Hospital. From this, it can be inferred that the bandits who kidnapped Zhang this time are the same gang who killed Zhou and Wei. The detectives later found two sets of wonton-selling equipment left behind by the kidnappers next to the Zhengyi Opera House and, along with the handgun, took them back to the police station, reported to the police chief, and informed all police stations to strictly pursue the escaped bandits.

Return of Savings from the Three Northeastern Provinces

Registration Has Begun

Storage and Exchange Bureau Announces Repayment Methods

After the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau received approval from the Ministry of Communications to repay savings from the three northeastern provinces, Mr. Fang Tinghua, Director of the Savings Department of the Bureau, drafted repayment regulations and registration procedures. The bureau will notify the regional postal administrations today and simultaneously announce the repayment regulations and begin registration. The details are as follows:

Postal Administration Notice: For the purpose of notification, all depositors holding savings passbooks or fixed deposit certificates issued by various bureaus in the Liaoning postal area before July 23, 1932, and in the Jilin and Heilongjiang postal areas before July 25, 1932, must register in person or through their agents at the bureau. This is a notice to inform everyone.

Repayment Regulations: (1) For passbook savings, depositors may register their savings passbooks at any post office (excluding branch offices) that handles passbook savings. For fixed deposit certificates, registration should be done at the post office (excluding branch offices) that handles fixed deposits. (2) If depositors wish to leave their savings with the post office, the registered post office will issue new deposit certificates one month after registration. For savings originally deposited in Hanyang currency in the Jilin and Heilongjiang areas, if the savings passbook and deposit certificate do not specify silver dollars, they will be converted to silver dollars at an 80% discount. Interest on these retained savings will be calculated from the day after the last interest settlement date of the Northeast Three Provinces Post Office (i.e., from July 1, 1932). Interest on fixed deposits will be calculated from the original deposit date at the original interest rate. (3) If depositors wish to withdraw these savings, they must also wait one month after registration. They can then apply to the original registered bureau for a withdrawal form according to the usual practice, and withdraw the savings with their savings passbook or fixed deposit certificate. All withdrawal forms and fixed deposit certificates must bear the original seal of the depositor. The interest on all withdrawn savings will be calculated up to the registration date according to the method described in section 2 above. (4) If deemed necessary, the post office may require depositors to provide a reliable guarantor before repaying the savings. (5) All savings repayment matters will be handled at the original registered bureau. If the original savings were deposited in Hanyang currency (see section 2 above), repayment will be made in silver dollars at an 80% discount.

Scope of Registration: According to Mr. Fang Tinghua, Director of the Savings Department, speaking to a reporter from the Huadong News Agency, all registration certificates and other items have been printed with designs and distributed to the postal administrations for printing. This is to facilitate depositors in obtaining and filling them out. To facilitate depositors, registration can be done in Tianjin, Beiping, Hankou, Qingdao, Shanghai, Guangdong, and other postal areas that handle postal remittances. The total amount to be repaid this time is approximately 230,000 yuan.

Strictly Prohibit Soliciting Donations Under False Pretenses

The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau issued instructions to various public organizations yesterday: "It is hereby notified that a letter from the Public Security Bureau, Law No. 259, states: 'The Northeast Volunteer Army Relief Association has written to the Public Security Bureau stating that the association has entrusted major banks, newspapers, and legal public organizations in Shanghai and other ports to collect donations for the Northeast Volunteer Army, and has never sent anyone to solicit donations in public. Recently, it has been heard that some unscrupulous individuals are using the association's name to solicit donations from shops and residents, going door-to-door. Such fraudulent behavior will inevitably waste the money obtained on improper purposes. If not strictly prohibited, it will discourage patriotic and willing donors. Therefore, this bureau is requested to instruct various district offices that anyone soliciting donations in the name of the association is an imposter and should be severely punished according to the law to deter wrongdoers and maintain the rule of law, etc.' Approved. In addition to instructing all subordinates to comply with and pay attention to investigating and apprehending, a corresponding letter is hereby sent to you for your reference and for you to instruct various agricultural, commercial, and industrial organizations to be informed to avoid being deceived. This is hereby instructed. Approved. In addition to separate instructions, the association is hereby informed to instruct various associations that if the above-mentioned fraudulent donation solicitation occurs, the witnesses should be sent to the nearest police station for investigation and prosecution. This is hereby ordered."

Zhou Yiting

Forensic Examination of a Death from Severe Injuries

Zhou Yiting, also known as Lao Wu, a native of Nanjing who was responsible for distributing Shanghai's major and minor newspapers for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou railways, was attacked with an axe by an assailant early yesterday morning around six o'clock. He sustained severe injuries to his head and shoulders as he left his residence and walked to the boundary road. The perpetrator managed to escape, and the police force was notified to send someone to the Renji Hospital for treatment. Zhou Yiting eventually died. His body was transported to the Forensic Examination Office on Feren Road. The details have already been published in yesterday's newspaper. This morning around ten o'clock, Guo Wei, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctor Zhang Yan and clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the office to examine the body. The case was opened, and Zhou Li, the wife of the deceased, testified that she was 43 years old and that the deceased was her husband. She said that he was usually kind and did not have any grudges against anyone. She said that someone had previously given him trouble one or two years ago regarding newspaper matters and that she suspected that this incident was related. She added that she was still asleep at the time and was initially unaware of the unfortunate event. She requested justice and the release of the body. In addition, Hua Men, a Western investigator, reported the details of the investigation at the time and presented the axe and the damaged hat. Prosecutor Guo, having heard the testimonies, ordered that the body of Zhou Yiting was indeed severely injured by an axe to the head and shoulders, leading to death. The body was released to his wife, Zhou Li, who signed a document for its return for burial. The police will strictly investigate the perpetrator and bring them to justice. The axe will be temporarily held by the police for safekeeping.

North Suzhou Road

Illegal Opium Pill Manufacturing Operation Busted

Bai Fujin, a Chinese detective with the Shanghai Municipal Police, learned that someone was secretly manufacturing and selling opium pills at No. 7 North Suzhou Road. Yesterday morning at 6:50 AM, he led a team of Chinese detectives to raid the premises. They arrested Wang Qishan from Shanxi, who was involved in the manufacturing, and six accomplices: Wang Mingshou, Shi Chengfang, Fan Zhenhai, Hao Yonghua, and Song Anfu. They confiscated a large quantity of white pills and white powder and brought them back to the police station. This morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stated the charges and requested a postponement because the confiscated pills needed to be sent to the Shanghai Municipal Council's Health Department for analysis of opium content. When questioned, Wang Qishan claimed that the pills were made from coffee extract and could be used as a smoking cessation product and not an opium substitute. The others were evasive. After reviewing the evidence, Judge Liu YuGui ordered Wang and the other six suspects to be detained for seven days for further questioning.

Thug Lu Chuanda Assassinated

Serious Injuries

Two assassination attempts occurred in the area under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai Municipal Police yesterday morning and evening. One was Zhou Yiting, also known as Lao Wu, a newspaper vendor on the railway lines, who was killed at the intersection of Shanqing Lane on the boundary road at 6:30 AM. The details have already been reported in this newspaper. The other involved Lu Chuanda, a local, who was suddenly attacked by three thugs with sharp blades and axes on Santai Road at 8:20 PM, sustaining injuries to his shoulders and legs. He was seriously injured and is currently being treated at Renji Hospital. It is understood that the victim, Lu Chuanda, is an unemployed thug who frequents tea houses and taverns in the Shanghai Municipal Police area. He is known for causing trouble and does not have a proper occupation. Yesterday afternoon around 6:00 PM, Lu had an argument with Li Acai, a native of Ningbo, over some matter, which escalated into a physical fight. The two were taken to the police station, where they were reprimanded by the police chief before being released. However, at 8:30 PM, Lu was walking on Santai Road when three thugs suddenly blocked his path. Each of them wielding axes, sharp blades, and handguns, they attacked Lu indiscriminately, resulting in severe injuries and heavy bleeding, causing him to collapse on the ground. The perpetrators fled. After being reported to the Shanghai Municipal Police, detectives Fang Qingyun and Bao Xiezhiguang were dispatched to investigate. They found Lu with a knife wound on his right shoulder and two axe wounds on his right leg, lying in a pool of blood. An axe was found nearby. Lu was taken to Renji Hospital for treatment, and the axe was taken back to the police station. The investigation began, and around 11:00 PM, Li Acai and Xia Shangde, two suspects, were apprehended at No. 51 North Shanxi Road. Later, a third accomplice, Ni Shengfu, a local, was apprehended at No. 68 Santai Road. They were taken back to the police station and detained separately. This morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Wang Yaotang, the police lawyer, stated the above circumstances, saying that the three defendants still needed to be investigated, so no charges had been filed and he requested detention. When questioned, Li Acai claimed that he had nothing to do with the incident, as Lu Chuanda had been his friend for several years and there was no animosity between them. He asserted that it was actually Lu's brother, Lu Touda, who committed the act and that he was being falsely accused. After Judge Liu YuGui reviewed the evidence, he ordered Li Acai and the other two suspects to be detained for seven days for further questioning after Lu Chuanda recovers from his injuries.

Discussions

What Do We Believe In?

— Tianfang

"A nation exists between heaven and earth, it must have something to stand on." A nation's spirit, though not necessarily identical to other nations, must at least be consistent within itself. Japan's "Yamato spirit," England's "John Bull," the German national spirit, and the Soviet Union's socialist ideology, regardless of whether they are correct or blindly adopted, can all influence a nation's actions and compete on the international stage. But what central idea do we have to lead our people's struggle?

One might answer: "We believe in Heaven." "Relying on Heaven for food" is the only philosophy of the Chinese people. This is evident in everyday life and doesn't need to be sought in old books.

But if everyone "relies on Heaven for food," there wouldn't be much of a problem. Unfortunately, some people are unwilling to "rely on Heaven" and want to "act on behalf of Heaven." As a result, others who want to "rely on Heaven" find it difficult to "get food." This is truly not accidental.

The severity of the current national crisis is undeniable. But to find a way out of this crisis, we cannot rely on "Heaven." However, the idea of "relying on Heaven for food" is pervading society. Although I am not a pessimist, the facts tell me that I cannot be optimistic. The entire country is in a state of bewilderment and confusion. The conscious are a minority within a minority. The majority of the working masses have not yet reached a full understanding of themselves, while a portion of the petite bourgeoisie cleverly evades reality and their historical responsibilities, hiding in an "ivory tower." Therefore, we currently lack a central idea that can serve as a standard for our national actions. We have lost our support, our faith, and are simply living "aimlessly." All we have are idle hopes, such as hoping for an earthquake to strike the enemy, or a revolution to break out in the enemy country within ten years, and decadent ideas, such as saving the country through dancing, saving the country through beauty, etc. These are all applications of the "relying on Heaven" philosophy, which is a natural reaction from a hopeless people who have been stimulated.

But are we just going to wander aimlessly like this? No, there are still many who are asleep, but there are also those who are awake, waiting for an effort.

Wasn't it Napoleon who said, "There is a giant in the East, let him sleep, for when he wakes, he will shake the world." Indeed, we have a population of 400 million, and our potential is unimaginable. But whoever can use an idea to connect our fragmented hearts is worthy of greatness. It is better to die with purpose than to live lazily. It is better to sacrifice with purpose than to survive aimlessly. Rise up!

In conclusion, the survival of China depends on whether many people can have their hearts connected. The shaking of the world depends on what kind of idea connects the hearts of the Chinese people.

My Dream

— Bing

According to scientific explanations, dreaming at night is a recurrence of daytime thoughts, or at least a result of being stimulated by moving environments. Therefore, dreams, originally an elusive and illusory state, are a kind of objective reaction. But since ancient times, there have been so-called "a dream of yellow millet" and "a dream of Nanke," the tone of which is completely unreal and缥缈. Even so, I wholeheartedly hope that my dream has some possibility of realization.

Let's first talk about the dream of my private life: Naturally, individuals living in the modern era are closely connected with society. In other words, individual life is invariably dominated by the times, just as individuals are clumps of grass in the vast wilderness, and the times are storms in all directions. See how the movement of the grass is dominated by the storm. However, I must always grasp it and be a person in the modern era. Whether using my brain or strength, I must grit my teeth and seek life through labor. People who sit around and eat are not only not allowed by the times and will be on the decline, but also inevitably destroy the inherent abilities of mankind. Cattle and horses can provide labor, and even chickens and dogs, though they can only eat human food, also have their contributions to society.

Moreover, I have no inherited wealth, nor do I have connections with powerful relatives. And I am so clumsy by nature, unable to flatter or please, not used to bragging or buttering up. In short, I hate any kind of scheming in my life. So, to live and not suffer from cold or hunger, I must have my own way of grasping things. I only hope that from now on, I can increase my ability to endure hardship. This is the prerequisite guarantee that my private life can be resolved.

Next, let's talk about society, which is so extensive that I can only extract the essence and briefly mention a few things:

I don't dream of a world of great harmony with no war, I only hope that future wars in the world, and even the operation of politics and the manipulation of economics, will gradually move towards a broader path.

I don't dream that the ruling class will completely stop exploiting, not want money, and that the common people will not have to fulfill their obligations or pay taxes. I only hope that under the beautiful name of abolishing exorbitant taxes, we don't repeat the famous couplet: "Never heard of taxes on manure since ancient times, only farts are not allowed to be donated today."

I don't dream that our country's higher education will be as effective as that of Britain and the United States, or that compulsory education will be as popular as that of Denmark. I only hope that every college student wearing a square hat can write a clear and fluent letter home, and that the number of illiterate people in the country will not increase to 100%.

I don't dream that our country is still the world's leading agricultural country, I only hope that from now on, we will no longer import food from abroad.

I don't dream that our country's industry will be as novel and widespread as that of Germany, I only hope that we can manufacture some of the pens that I am now holding to write with, so that I don't have to use these infuriating foreign goods anymore.

I don't dream that businessmen will rise up to resist enemy goods, I only hope that they will not secretly replace some domestic goods with enemy brands and sell them. When the anti-Japanese tension is high, they switch the enemy goods to domestic brands.

I don't dream that all doctors can cure all diseases, I only hope that they will not arbitrarily treat and kill people.

I don't dream that all 400 million of our compatriots will resist Japan, I only hope that the pro-Japanese traitors will not emerge endlessly, making foreigners laugh and harming our compatriots, that would be enough.

I don't dream that the tram will not increase prices when copper coins become cheaper, I only hope that when copper coins become more expensive, there will be a day when prices are reduced.

Finally, I don't dream that all my dreams can be realized, I only hope that there is some possibility of their realization.

President Wang Returns to China

Cannot Guess Their Psychology

— Xiying

Every morning, rain or shine, on the tram, one always has the pleasure of appreciating the demeanor of a few female office workers. They bear the important responsibility of raising women's rights and implementing gender equality, so they would rather abandon their boudoirs and spend their lives as female office workers in the crowded market. They are not doing it for a meager monthly salary, nor do they deign to be called living advertisements or vases, new terms. Their sole purpose is to open up a new path for the women's community and give the men a head start. Therefore, they are often aloof and arrogant, and do not take any of the men in the world seriously. They seem to mean: even if we can't marry you smelly men, we don't have to worry about starving to death. We have the ability to support ourselves, but you can't find us as wives, so you have to get anxious! However, seeing them change their clothes every day and always apply red and white patches on their faces, one can't help but wonder whether they are specifically demonstrating to the men, or whether they are indicating that female office workers must be like this. At that time, I am afraid that they all hope to be favored by a rich man like the so-called ××× female郎 in ×× company, to be a lady with fur coat and pearls! After all, what they think in their hearts is something we cannot guess.

Novels

Fleeting Moments in a Dream (Continued 10)

— Qin Shouou

Speak of Cao Cao, and Cao Cao arrives; it was indeed Lin Daping.

Young people, when they meet, are as easily blended as hot water and milk. Moreover, today they had a legitimate business to discuss, making their conversation even more lively. Lin Daping spoke the most, explaining the entire plan for establishing the record company as if he were telling a story, every word exceptionally pleasing to the ear.

"I will draft a contract tomorrow, and then we can formally begin!" After much idle talk, the lawyer Wang, well-versed in legal knowledge, decided on a concrete plan.

Wu Yi, being the most straightforward and quick-tongued of the lot, told Zhao Qianli everything about the matter in the editorial office that very night. Coincidentally, Zhao Qianli had been feeling down lately and wanted to find something to do for leisure, so he volunteered to Wu Yi, expressing his willingness to join their partnership.

……………………

After the establishment of the "Great King Record Company," Wu Yi seemed like a changed man. He spent his free time lingering there. Not only was he no longer as financially strapped as he used to be, feeling like he was constantly preparing for New Year's Eve, but also mentally, he felt extremely comfortable, happy, and content.

"I have three of the best friends, they are all equally enthusiastic and loyal!" He once said proudly to someone, "Now, I am beginning to taste the true joy of making friends!"

(7) The Actress

One early winter morning, around ten o'clock, Wu Yi was lying quietly on a velvet sofa in the manager's office of the Great King Record Company, flipping through the day's newspapers. Because it was so early, neither Wang Yulin nor Zhao Qianli had arrived, and even Lin Daping, the manager, had not yet made his appearance.

"Excuse me! Is Mr. Lin at home?" Wu Yi was studying a telegram from Army A denouncing Army B, much like one would study ancient texts, when suddenly, the small door with opaque glass opened halfway. In a strong scent of perfume essence, a beautiful woman, tall and graceful, with picturesque eyebrows and eyes, walked in. Instantly, the room brightened as if a five-hundred-candlepower electric light had been turned on, almost blinding Wu Yi.

In the previous years, Wu Yi had clashed with the fairer sex over a thousand times, and images of women had almost filled his brain. However, this one before him truly possessed a wonderful demeanor he had never seen in his life. Especially when she smiled, the two dimples on her cheeks, like being molded from powder and carved from jade, almost made him wonder if he was dreaming!

"He hasn't arrived yet, but he might be here soon," Wu Yi stood up and replied politely.

"Then... would it be possible for me to wait here for a while?" This young lady was not only beautiful but also wonderfully generous. She slightly bent one leg forward, performed a curtsy commonly used by noblewomen in the seventeenth century, and briskly removed a fur-collared cloak, revealing a pure black dress.
